## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the right-hand side of a population dynamics ODE. Classical models range from simple exponential/logistic growth to more complex forms with Allee effects, time-dependent parameters, or oscillatory forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth decelerating logarithmically near capacity)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * P * (1 - c1 * P) (growth rate proportional to P^2 at low density)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (saturating per-capita growth rate)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (time-varying growth rate)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (shifting environment)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (logistic growth with Holling type II removal)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power growth dynamics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Cubic polynomial in P (terms P, P², P³) → Allee effect or bistability in population dynamics
- Product of P with (1 - c*P) → logistic-type density dependence with a carrying capacity
- Logarithmic dependence log(c/P) → Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate decreases logarithmically
- Sinusoidal dependence on t multiplied by growth terms → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing
- Ratio P/(c + P) in growth or mortality terms → Holling type II functional response / saturating interaction
- Per-capita growth rate (dP_dt / P) that is linear in P → classic logistic model structure
- Per-capita growth rate that is nonlinear/concave in P → generalized density dependence (theta-logistic)
- Difference of two power laws (P^a - P^b) → competing anabolic vs catabolic processes
- Absence of explicit t dependence → autonomous ODE, population dynamics determined solely by current state
- Multiplicative factor (P - c) with c > 0 → critical population threshold (Allee effect / minimum viable population)

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(t, P) = 0.1404 \cdot (-1 + P/4.532) \cdot (1 - P/78.49) \cdot P + 0.1404 \cdot P / t^{4.532}$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49) = -1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)$$

So the GT becomes:
$$0.1404 \cdot P \cdot \left(-1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)\right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

$$= 0.1404 \cdot \left(-P + P^2/78.49 + P^2/4.532 - P^3/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)\right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

This simplifies to:
$$= a \cdot P^3 + b \cdot P^2 + c \cdot P + d \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

where:
- $a = -0.1404/(4.532 \times 78.49) \approx -3.949 \times 10^{-4}$
- $b = 0.1404 \cdot (1/78.49 + 1/4.532) \approx 0.1404 \cdot 0.2334 \approx 0.03277$
- $c = -0.1404$
- $d = 0.1404$

So the GT has the **structural form**:
$$\boxed{P^3 \cdot c_0 + P^2 \cdot c_1 + P \cdot c_2 + P \cdot c_3 \cdot t^{c_4}}$$

Now let me check each candidate against this form.

### Candidate 1: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 \log(P c_3 + 1) + P c_4 (c_5 + t)^{c_6} + c_7/(c_8 + t)^5$
Contains $\log$ terms and $(c_5+t)^{c_6}$ instead of $t^{c_4}$. The $\log$ term cannot be zeroed without losing the $P^3$ term. Missing $P^3$. If we set $c_2 = 0$, we lose the log but then we only have $P^2$ and $P$ polynomial terms, missing $P^3$. Also $(c_5+t)^{c_6}$: if $c_5=0$, this becomes $t^{c_6}$, which works. But we still need $P^3$.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 (c_3 + t)^{c_4} + P c_5 \log(P c_6 + 1)$
Has $\log$ term. Setting $c_5 = 0$ removes it, but then no $P^3$ term. Cannot match.

### Candidate 3: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + P^2 c_2 + P c_3 + P c_4 + P^{c_5} c_6 t^{c_7} + c_8 t^{c_9}$
$P^2 c_1 + P^2 c_2 = P^2(c_1+c_2)$, $P c_3 + P c_4 = P(c_3+c_4)$. The term $P^{c_5} c_6 t^{c_7}$: we need $P \cdot t^{c_4}$, so set $c_5 = 1$, giving $c_6 \cdot P \cdot t^{c_7}$. ### Candidate 32: $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_3 + P^2 c_4 + P c_5 + P c_6 t^{c_7} + P c_8 + c_9 t^{c_7}}{P c_1 + c_2}$
This is a rational function. GT is polynomial in P (plus $P t^{c}$). For this to match, the denominator must divide the numerator exactly. Let's denote $D = c_1 P + c_2$. We need:
$$\frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_3+c_4)P^2 + (c_5+c_8)P + c_6 P t^{c_7} + c_9 t^{c_7}}{c_1 P + c_2}$$

For this to equal $aP^3 + bP^2 + cP + dPt^e$, we'd need the denominator to be a constant (set $c_1=0$), giving everything divided by $c_2$. Then: $\frac{c_0}{c_2}P^3 + \frac{c_3+c_4}{c_2}P^2 + \frac{c_5+c_8}{c_2}P + \frac{c_6}{c_2}Pt^{c_7} + \frac{c_9}{c_2}t^{c_7}$.

The last term $\frac{c_9}{c_2}t^{c_7}$ is not in GT (it's not multiplied by P). Set $c_9=0$. Then it matches!
Candidate 32 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 33: $P c_0 + P c_1 t^{c_2} + c_3 \log(P c_4+1) + c_5 + c_6 \log(c_7 \exp(P c_8)+1)$
Set $c_3=0, c_5=0, c_6=0$: $P c_0 + P c_1 t^{c_2}$. Missing $P^3, P^2$. No match.
Candidate 33 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 34: $P^2 c_0 \exp(c_1 t) + P c_2 + P c_3 t^{c_4} + P^{c_5} c_6$
Set $c_1=0$: $c_0 P^2$. Set $c_5=3$: $c_6 P^3$. Result: $c_6 P^3 + c_0 P^2 + c_2 P + c_3 P t^{c_4}$. Matches!
Candidate 34 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 35: $P c_0 + P c_1 t^{c_2} + P c_3 (P c_4)^{c_5} + P c_6 + c_7 \exp(P c_8) + c_9$
$P c_3 (P c_4)^{c_5} = c_3 c_4^{c_5} P^{1+c_5}$. Set $c_5=2$: $\alpha P^3$. Set $c_7=0, c_9=0$. Result: $\alpha P^3 + (c_0+c_6)P + c_1 P t^{c_2}$. Missing $P^2$. Hmm, we need $P^2$. Can we get it? No other term can produce $P^2$. No match.

Wait, actually we could set $c_5$ to something else. If $c_5=1$: $\alpha P^2$, but then no $P^3$. We can only get one power from this term. Missing either $P^3$ or $P^2$.
Candidate 35 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 40: $\frac{P \cdot P^{c_0} c_1 + P c_4 + P c_5 t^{c_6} + P^{c_0} c_7 + c_8 t^{c_6}}{P c_2 + c_3}$
Set $c_2=0$: divide by $c_3$. Then: $\frac{c_1}{c_3} P^{1+c_0} + \frac{c_4}{c_3} P + \frac{c_5}{c_3} P t^{c_6} + \frac{c_7}{c_3} P^{c_0} + \frac{c_8}{c_3} t^{c_6}$.
Set $c_0=2$: $\frac{c_1}{c_3} P^3 + \frac{c_7}{c_3} P^2 + \frac{c_4}{c_3} P + \frac{c_5}{c_3} P t^{c_6} + \frac{c_8}{c_3} t^{c_6}$.
Set $c_8=0$. Result: $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P + \delta P t^{c_6}$. Matches!
Candidate 40 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 44: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 (P c_3)^{c_4} + P c_5 t^{c_6} + P c_7$
$P c_2 (P c_3)^{c_4} = c_2 c_3^{c_4} P^{1+c_4}$. Set $c_4=2$: $\alpha P^3$. Result: $\alpha P^3 + c_0 P^2 + (c_1+c_7)P + c_5 P t^{c_6}$. Matches!
Candidate 44 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 45: $P c_0 + P c_1 t^{c_2} + P c_3 (P c_4+1)^2 + c_5$
$P c_3 (P c_4+1)^2 = P c_3 (P^2 c_4^2 + 2P c_4 + 1) = c_3 c_4^2 P^3 + 2c_3 c_4 P^2 + c_3 P$.
Set $c_5=0$. Result: $c_3 c_4^2 P^3 + 2c_3 c_4 P^2 + (c_0+c_3)P + c_1 P t^{c_2}$.
This has the right form, but the coefficients of $P^3$ and $P^2$ are linked: if $P^3$ coeff is $c_3 c_4^2$ and $P^2$ coeff is $2c_3 c_4$, then $P^2$ coeff $= 2\sqrt{c_3 \cdot P^3\text{coeff}}$... Actually, we need to check if we can independently set $P^3$ and $P^2$ coefficients.

GT values: $P^3$ coeff $\approx -3.949 \times 10^{-4}$, $P^2$ coeff $\approx 0.03277$.

We need $c_3 c_4^2 = -3.949 \times 10^{-4}$ and $2c_3 c_4 = 0.03277$.

From the second: $c_3 c_4 = 0.01639$. From the first: $c_4 = -3.949 \times 10^{-4}/0.01639 = -0.02410$.
Then $c_3 = 0.01639/(-0.02410) = -0.6801$.
Check: $c_3 c_4^2 = -0.6801 \times 0.000581 = -3.95 \times 10^{-4}$. ✓

So the coefficients CAN be independently matched! Matches!
Candidate 45 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 46: $P c_0 + P c_1 t^{c_2} + P c_3 (P c_4+1)^{c_5} + c_6$
Set $c_6=0$. $P c_3 (P c_4+1)^{c_5}$: this is $c_3 P (c_4 P + 1)^{c_5}$. For this to produce $P^3 + P^2 + P$ polynomial, we'd need $c_5$ to be a positive integer. Set $c_5=2$: same as Candidate 45. Matches (as shown above)!
